      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780755334124" href="/book/show/597642.Fragile_Things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-challenge">fantasy-sci-fi-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=quirky">quirky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=neil-gaiman">neil-gaiman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=alphabet-challenge">alphabet-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448054278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16105435787744735591"><br/>Stories, Neil Gaiman informs in the introduction, are fragile things made up of 26 letters (more if you want to use phonetic symbols), ink and paper. They are illusions created by things that cannot last, but the best stories survive and transform. The stories within this volume are perhaps some of those best stories.<br/><br/>This collection contained many of Gaiman's most famous short stories. I want to write three quick reviews of some of the short stories. Including one which I previously read online </span>
  <span id="freeText16105435787744735591" style="display:none"><br />Stories, Neil Gaiman informs in the introduction, are fragile things made up of 26 letters (more if you want to use phonetic symbols), ink and paper. They are illusions created by things that cannot last, but the best stories survive and transform. The stories within this volume are perhaps some of those best stories.<br /><br />This collection contained many of Gaiman's most famous short stories. I want to write three quick reviews of some of the short stories. Including one which I previously read online and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300893787" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewed seperately</a>.<br /><br /><b>A Study in Emerald</b><br /><br />A re-read of A Study in Emerald proved highly enlightening as I was able to observe and analyse the technique used by Gaiman in creating the story. As previously mentioned his first paragraph verges close to plagiarism in how it replicates the feel of another Sherlock Holmes story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/102868.A_Study_in_Scarlet__Sherlock_Holmes___1_" title="A Study in Scarlet (Sherlock Holmes, #1) by Arthur Conan Doyle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Study in Scarlet</a>. Yet only a foolish person would dare call this a work of plagiarism, rather it is a story which clearly references both Lovecraft and Doyle in a unique manner. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That twist with having Moriarty and his accomplice be the heroes is fantastic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It is a work of genius and a very clever short story in all its technical proficiency.<br /><br /><b>Forbidden Brides of the Faceless Slaves in the Secret House of the Night of Dread Desire</b> <br /><br />This was a story which I didn't quite understand but I have an idea of what Gaiman was aiming at. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think his story was set in a macabre fantasy horror world with the author trying to write 'real life' fiction. Meaning he was actually writing gothic horror. And fantasy to him was writing about our real world. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> If what I think is correct then it was a very clever story, speaking about the writer's art and about the connection between horror and reality. It was also a creepy story in the proper way a horror story should be!<br /><br /><b>The Problem of Susan</b><br /><br />This is one of Neil Gaiman's more famous stories and also a very controversial one. I liked some elements of it, for instance the technical aspect of the writing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and the hint that the woman being interviewed was Susan. I also liked the suggestion that perhaps Susan was left behind for a purpose at that time in the Narnia books though I doubt I agree. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However what did not work where the sexual undertones and the analysis that Susan was left behind because of her growing sexuality which is what many people have criticised Lewis for. However I think that section of The last Battle personally is meant to be focused around the fact that Susan became focused on other things than Narnia. I think that Lewis merely phrased this concept awkwardly, in a way that makes it easy to see it as a sexist dig at Susan not being able to go to Narnia because she discovered boys and lipstick. Yet if you do a true analysis I think you'll notice that the grown up Lucy does go to Narnia in the end. Surely she would have discovered some kind of adult sexuality? Yet she remained true to Narnia. I also disliked the metaphor with the lion and the witch very much. I think Neil Gaiman's own personal ideology causes him to spite the religious message in the Narnia books and that it was rather apparent in his (I thought it was vulgar) portrayal of the witch and lion.<br /><br /><b>Conclusion</b><br /><br />On the whole most of the stories worked and the poems additionally added an extra level to this collection. It is certainly something every short story enthusiast and fantasy fan, let alone Neil Gaiman fan will want to read. Gaiman is one of the more versatile modern authors and his work is both bizarre, fascinating, reflective and full of literary reference. His humour shines through in subtle ways, making his work that little bit more charming. On the whole an easy four star rating and a collection to enjoy on any kind of day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16105435787744735591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_847278317" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847278317" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/847278317?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060515232" href="/book/show/7061309-fragile-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=shortstories-collections">shortstories-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847278317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13328822547853874136">This is my second read-through of this book, and it was just as great, and oddly, just as surprising this time around as the last. <br/><br/>I don't know why it is, but I just have this image in my mind of Neil Gaiman as a proper author. I don't mean 'proper' to mean that he is officially an author (though he is), or that he does it correctly (though he does), but 'proper' in terms of vocabulary and ideas being more on the... non-vulgar side of things. I have this picture in my head, despite reading his b</span>
  <span id="freeText13328822547853874136" style="display:none">This is my second read-through of this book, and it was just as great, and oddly, just as surprising this time around as the last. <br /><br />I don't know why it is, but I just have this image in my mind of Neil Gaiman as a proper author. I don't mean 'proper' to mean that he is officially an author (though he is), or that he does it correctly (though he does), but 'proper' in terms of vocabulary and ideas being more on the... non-vulgar side of things. I have this picture in my head, despite reading his books and stories and blog posts and comics, and having seen him live with his wife Amanda Palmer, who seems to revel in vulgarity at times... and none of these things support this idea I have of him. But still it persists. <br /><br />And so when I read the stories in this book, they give me a little thrill, because I don't expect the vulgar and the so-very-adult-ness of some of these stories. Even though, by all accounts, I SHOULD.<br /><br />I'm not easily shocked or offended, but I like that sometimes Neil's writing van cause that little thrill in me. It keeps me on my toes. Doesn't let me get too comfortable in Neil's work, because there's such a huge range of it that you never know which way he'll go next. And I like that. A lot. <br /><br />I don't know if I want to talk about the stories individually, except to say that I don't think there's any that I actively dislike, though I'd have to say that Harlequin Valentine is probably my least favorite. But I do want to say that one thing I love about almost the entire collection is the interpretability of the stories. They all have layers that just work so beautifully together, and you can see them in the way that makes sense to you. <br /><br />The stories aren't surprisingly good, because I expect everything Neil writes to be good, but they are surprising AND good. So many of these stories gave me an interesting perspective on something, and made me a part of the story for a little while. Really excellent short fiction pulls you into the story and doesn't want to let you go. You want to think about it, and examine it, and expand on it... and that's what this collection achieved. <br /><br />This is a fantastic collection, and if you can get this on audio, I highly recommend it. Of course, Neil Gaiman could read a Chinese take-out menu and I'll fall all over myself gushing about how brilliantly he read it. So, you know, listen to it. You won't be sorry. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13328822547853874136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39028139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39028139" />
    <a title="Kerfe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/412055-kerfe"><img alt="Kerfe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317990187p2/412055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39028139?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerfe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerfe" href="/user/show/412055-kerfe">Kerfe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/412055-kerfe?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/412055-kerfe?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39028139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9608398009075933998">I have not read Neil Gaiman's novels but I've heard good things about them. This collection is obviously not a good place to start reading his work. First off, the intro was irritating. The self-satisfied aren't-I-wonderful? name dropping tone was kind of overbearing, and probably put me in an extra-critical mood. <br/><br/>The short story is unforgiving; you don't have time for slow bits, or parts that sound like you've read them already somewhere before. And paying homage is tricky too--it can't be mere</span>
  <span id="freeText9608398009075933998" style="display:none">I have not read Neil Gaiman's novels but I've heard good things about them. This collection is obviously not a good place to start reading his work. First off, the intro was irritating. The self-satisfied aren't-I-wonderful? name dropping tone was kind of overbearing, and probably put me in an extra-critical mood. <br /><br />The short story is unforgiving; you don't have time for slow bits, or parts that sound like you've read them already somewhere before. And paying homage is tricky too--it can't be merely a lesser or different version of the original concept. It needs to have its own substance, its own reason for being. Gaiman seems to admire science fiction, horror, and fantasy, but his attempts to emulate them failed to engage me.<br /><br />Maybe the real world has made me too cynical or jaded, but what is meant to be scary or sinister seems here to be instead pathetic and old. What should be mysterious is merely another plot for a reality TV show. The writing itself is not that good, and uses an awful lot of cliches, in a kind of casual, isn't this amusing? way. If Gaiman is trying to parody pop culture, it falls flat for me. It's just not different or new or clever enough.<br /><br />Despite my overall disappointment, there were some things I liked, especially the science fictiony "Goliath" (inspired by the Matrix movies) and "How to Talk to Girls at Parties". The American Gods novella, "Monarch of the Glen", also had some good parts, which leads me to believe that the novels really must be far better. The poetry did not appeal to me, except for "Instructions".<br /><br />I know publishers like to cash in on popular authors, but if, like me, this is the first Gaiman you pick up, it's doubtful it would make you want to read more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9608398009075933998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1286358788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286358788" />
    <a title="Erica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2644090-erica"><img alt="Erica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558548351p2/2644090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286358788?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica" href="/user/show/2644090-erica">Erica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4934443986381538935">Wow, I am crabby.<br/>I'm in a punching kittens/kicking puppies place right now, have been for awhile.<br/>I think this current state of being is blocking my ability to find enjoyment in things I typically find delightful.<br/>This book of collected Gaiman stories, for example.<br/>I pressed "Play", he started reading, I went, "Ahhhhhhh. Bliss," and then I got bored.<br/>I made it all the way to the last disc and then kind of fast-forwarded to the end, skipping giant parts, leaving huge swaths of un-listened-to prose be</span>
  <span id="freeText4934443986381538935" style="display:none">Wow, I am crabby.<br />I'm in a punching kittens/kicking puppies place right now, have been for awhile.<br />I think this current state of being is blocking my ability to find enjoyment in things I typically find delightful.<br />This book of collected Gaiman stories, for example.<br />I pressed "Play", he started reading, I went, "Ahhhhhhh. Bliss," and then I got bored.<br />I made it all the way to the last disc and then kind of fast-forwarded to the end, skipping giant parts, leaving huge swaths of un-listened-to prose behind me.<br />It just didn't scratch the itch I'd expected to have relieved, which is tragic (for me)<br />Don't worry, I'm not losing the 1/4 soul I own (my mother told me my siblings and I share one soul between us because there aren't enough souls to go around anymore, due to our living too long and the lower infant mortality rate, etc. Damn you, medical technology, messing with the supply and demand of souls), it's just bruised right now and I need a breather.<br />I may try this again another day. Maybe not, though; I'd already read/heard/seen about half the stories anyhow so I'm not sure that I really need to go through it all again.<br />Man. I am so sad for myself.</span>

<div id="review_99879177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99879177" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99879177?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=shortstories-collections">shortstories-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99879177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4781503453225586810">I really enjoyed this collection of stories. I listened to the audiobook version read by the author himself, which I think added quite a bit to the experience. It's been my experience that authors who read their own stories as audiobooks are generally not the best. While it's true that they know their characters and their stories, many of them just don't have the voice or talent for oral storytelling. That's not to say that the author isn't a storyteller - obviously they are, often they just sho</span>
  <span id="freeText4781503453225586810" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this collection of stories. I listened to the audiobook version read by the author himself, which I think added quite a bit to the experience. It's been my experience that authors who read their own stories as audiobooks are generally not the best. While it's true that they know their characters and their stories, many of them just don't have the voice or talent for oral storytelling. That's not to say that the author isn't a storyteller - obviously they are, often they just shouldn't do it orally. <br /><br />Neil Gaiman, thankfully, is a natural oral storyteller. He brings the story and the characters to life, and the listener forgets that they are listening to something that was once written because it feels so naturally spoken -- like the story is just flowing through him to us. <br /><br />Many of these stories took me by surprise. I don't think of Gaiman as a YA author, but even so, I didn't expect the themes and details of the stories in this collection to be so jaded or brutal. Gaiman doesn't make these things the focus, but rather adds them in an almost nonchalant way that has more of an impact because it's NOT the focus. <br /><br />I also really enjoy Gaiman's perspective and unique way of seeing the world and everything in it. I like his ability to effortlessly maneuver his readers right into the position we need to be in for maximum effect, and when we get there, he flips everything, so we're left wondering just what happened and how we got where we are when obviously we were just on our way to somewhere else. <br /><br />I'm not much for poetry, and I didn't really get much out of the poems that were included here, so I couldn't give this one a 5 star rating, but aside from that, I loved this collection. It's a keeper. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4781503453225586810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1649561574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1649561574" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1649561574?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6225133-fragile-things">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1649561574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3405221231020936829"><b>Please note that I gave this 3.5 stars. I rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads.</b><br/><br/>So all in all definitely a mixed bag I am sad to say. I have loved everything else that I have read of Neil Gaiman's though I did only find Good Omens to be okay/good and have no intention of re-reading it. I have already read "Coraline" and "The Ocean at the End of the Lane" twice this year.<br/><br/>"A Study in Emerald" (5 stars)- a Sherlock Holmes story that is not a Sherlock Holmes story. I know that makes no sense, but yo</span>
  <span id="freeText3405221231020936829" style="display:none"><b>Please note that I gave this 3.5 stars. I rounded it up to 4 stars on Goodreads.</b><br /><br />So all in all definitely a mixed bag I am sad to say. I have loved everything else that I have read of Neil Gaiman's though I did only find Good Omens to be okay/good and have no intention of re-reading it. I have already read "Coraline" and "The Ocean at the End of the Lane" twice this year.<br /><br />"A Study in Emerald" (5 stars)- a Sherlock Holmes story that is not a Sherlock Holmes story. I know that makes no sense, but you will get that when you read the whole story. I really did enjoy this one especially about a darker version of the heroes we know and love. <br /><br />"The Fairy Reel" (4.5 stars)- I liked the poem and it did have me imagining a young man out in the woods calling to a fairy.<br /><br />"October in the Chair" (5 stars)-This was a great story involving the months as we know them coming to life and telling stories. <br /><br />"The Hidden Chamber" (3 stars)- I think I just dislike poems. I recall from Stephen King's latest he had some in there and I just hard cringed at them. <br /><br />"Forbidden Brides of the Faceless Slaves of the Secret House of the Night of Dread Desire" (3 stars)- I still have absolutely no idea what in the world was going on. We have a man writing a ghost story and oh yeah he may live in a haunted house. And people are not who they appear to be. And things just end on no explanation. <br /><br />"The Flints of Memory Lane" (4 stars)- Just a short story about a young man remembering the time he came across something evil. <br /><br />"Closing Time" (4.5 stars)- This story was a little weird, but in the end I liked it well enough. I think that the problem was the reveal just happens and I sat there scratching my head. So I don't know what the man in the story met as a young boy. <br /><br />"Going Wodwo" (1 star) -Another poem. At least it was only a page and a half. <br /><br />"Bitter Grounds" (2 stars)-This story seemed endless and nonsensical. I am still trying to figure out what happened to the anthropology professor so maybe that's why I could not get into this story.<br /><br />"Other People" (3 stars) - I was the least surprised person at the end of this short story. <br /><br />"Keepsakes and Treasures" (1 star)- I know that there are evil people in the world, but this whole story was repulsive as hell. I found it hard to read and hope that Mr. Alice and Mr. Smith show up again and something terrible happens to them both. <br /><br />"Good Boys Deserve Favors" (2 stars)- An okay story. I just didn't get the point of it. It stuck out a bit in this collection to me. <br /><br />"The Facts in the Case of the Departure of Miss Finch" (1 star)- This story was so odd. I don't even know what I was supposed to take away from it. Miss Finch sucks. But so do the other people in this story.<br /><br />"Strange Little Girls" (2 stars)- Just seemed to be listing different attributes certain women take on. I don't know. I didn't enjoy it. <br /><br />"Harlequin Valentine" (2 stars) - Meh. <br /><br />"Locks" (1 star) -Another poem. <br /><br />"The Problem of Susan" (5 stars)- Disturbing as anything, but it does give a different perspective as what became of Susan Pevensie and why she turned her back on all things Narnia. I do want to high five Mr. Gaiman for this one. It has never sat right for me that Susan was left behind to never enter Narnia because of some b.s. reasons.<br /><br />"Instructions" (1 star)- Another poem. <br /><br />"How Do You Think It Feels?" (3 stars)- I went back and forth on this one because I thought the main character was a jerk. And it seems in the end maybe he imagined things about a former lover. Who knows. <br /><br />"My Life" (1 star)- Another poem. <br /><br />"Fifteen Painted Cards from a Vampire Tarot" (1 star)- No. I just read that thing twice and just rolled my eyes.<br /><br />"Feeders and Eaters" (3 stars)- Another weird story. Why did the character of Eddie even get into the arrangement that he did. There were so many questions I had. I think the ending was supposed to shock, but I was left with a lot of questions. <br /><br />"Diseasemaker's Croup" (.5 star) - My eyes glazed over so I can't tell you what this was about. I tried to re-read it for the final review and my brain shut that down so quickly it was unreal. So that's all I got. I could not stand to read this past two paragraphs. <br /><br />"In the End" (1.5 stars)- Barely counts as a short story about the Garden of Eden. <br /><br />"Goliath" (4 stars)- Sad story from beginning to end. Now of course I am wondering what was real and what was not based on how the story went.<br /><br />"Pages from a Journal Found in a Shoebox Left in a Greyhound Bus Somewhere Between Tulsa, Oklahoma, and Louisville, Kentucky" (3.5 stars)-It was okay. I just didn't get into this story much.<br /><br />"How to Talk to Girls at Parties" (3 stars)-Very weird. I really didn't get into it at all. <br /><br />"The Day the Saucers Came" (4 stars)- I did like this long winding story where it comes out that sitting around and waiting for someone to call you is pretty much never the answer.<br /><br />"Sunbird" (4 stars)- I liked the whole thing about this elusive eating club getting their just desserts.<br /><br />"Inventing Aladdin" (3 stars)- Another poem taking a look at Scheherazade. This was one of the few poems in the collection that I enjoyed. <br /><br />"The Monarch of the Glen" (5 stars) -This is American Gods #1.5 and I will say that if I had gotten this as a stand alone novella I would have been happy. We get to revisit Shadow and see how he is faring. He comes across some things that should not be real and also the characters Mr. Alice and Mr. Smith from a previous story in this collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3405221231020936829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65003405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6805498032890093510">4.5 stars, really.<br/><br/>What a delightful collection of Gaiman's short stories! I was very impressed, liking this even better than I expected. It very nearly got a full 5-stars, but I honestly have a hard time giving that rating to a collection of short stories. They have to really 'wow' me for that. Most of the time the stories, being short, don't really capture the full suspension of belief that's required to become fully absorbed and lost. The more lost I get, the more big stars it'll get.<br/><br/>That said</span>
  <span id="freeText6805498032890093510" style="display:none">4.5 stars, really.<br /><br />What a delightful collection of Gaiman's short stories! I was very impressed, liking this even better than I expected. It very nearly got a full 5-stars, but I honestly have a hard time giving that rating to a collection of short stories. They have to really 'wow' me for that. Most of the time the stories, being short, don't really capture the full suspension of belief that's required to become fully absorbed and lost. The more lost I get, the more big stars it'll get.<br /><br />That said, this is still an excellent work. I had some hesitation, not to read it but certainly in prioritizing it, after I'd read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Smoke and Mirrors by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Smoke and Mirrors</a> a couple of years ago. I liked that collection, but it didn't grab me. Certainly not like I was grabbed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods" title="American Gods by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverwhere</a>, or the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23754.Preludes_and_Nocturnes__The_Sandman___1_" title="Preludes and Nocturnes (The Sandman, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludes and Nocturnes</a> (Sandman) series. But this one certainly did the trick and belongs in the Gaiman canon with those other heavy hitters.<br /><br />The poetry and other short miscellanies within this book were interesting, and some of them actually made sense (unlike poetry in general which usually comes off to me as fluff). They added a nice interlude between the stories, the meat of the matter.<br /><br />And those are what makes this a gem.<br /><br />"Monarch of the Glen" is a novella which serves as a sequel to <i>American Gods</i>. Here we get to see a little bit of how Shadow is carrying on after the events of that novel. This was a nice teaser, making me want a new American Gods novel now. C'mon, Neil. Everybody wants you to write it.<br /><br />"The Facts in the Case of the Departure of Miss Finch" is wonderful. Sinister and mysterious and weird.<br /><br />"The Problem of Susan" addresses some concerns with the Narnia series.<br /><br />"A Study in Emerald" is just wicked and delightful.<br /><br />"Goliath" is a nice surprise and very weirdly well done.<br /><br />"October in the Chair" has wonderful characterization and keeps the reader on the edge of his/her chair.<br /><br />"Bitter Grounds", "How to Talk to Girls at Parties", "Keepsakes and Treasures", and "Harlequin Valentine" were all favorites too. Though there really wasn't a bad one in the lot.<br /><br />Yes, it's definitely time for a new American Gods novel, and another story collection while you're at it, Mr. Gaiman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6805498032890093510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17099485984401067012">I finished "Fragile Things" by Neil Gaiman while I was waiting for the anesthesiologist at UCLA Medical Center. Two days later, while visiting me in the hospital, my daughter announced that she "stole" the book from me. So, I don't have it to refer back to while doing this review. <br/><br/>For me, the highlight of this collection of short stories and poems was the novella "Monarch of the Glen" that featured Shadow from "American Gods" re-interpreting the Beowulf legend. It was extremely good. I thought t</span>
  <span id="freeText17099485984401067012" style="display:none">I finished "Fragile Things" by Neil Gaiman while I was waiting for the anesthesiologist at UCLA Medical Center. Two days later, while visiting me in the hospital, my daughter announced that she "stole" the book from me. So, I don't have it to refer back to while doing this review. <br /><br />For me, the highlight of this collection of short stories and poems was the novella "Monarch of the Glen" that featured Shadow from "American Gods" re-interpreting the Beowulf legend. It was extremely good. I thought the poetry throughout the collection was very good too. The stories were kind of hit or miss. Right now, I really can't remember any except "How to Talk to Girls at Parties" which is about a socially inept young man from a boys' school who gets dragged to a party by his best friend and they end up at the wrong party. Let's just say that he learns to talk to girls, but they're the wrong kind of girls.<br /><br />All in all, I think "Fragile Things" is a good choice if you don't really have the attention span to devote to a novel at a given time and you just want some light reading that can be read in short spurts. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17099485984401067012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_30906648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30906648" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1433865-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254324661p2/1433865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30906648?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/1433865-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755334148" href="/book/show/862815.Fragile_Things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=short-fiction">short-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1433865-robert?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30906648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8956743607907853398">As with previous collections of short pieces by Gaiman, I found this extremely variable in quality: Anything referred to as "poetry" is execrable, as are all the "stories" that are extremely short and fail to follow any normal narrative structure. On the other hand, the pieces that follow some kind of conventional method are all at least OK and in some cases delightful. <br/><br/>Stand-out entries are A Study in Emerald and How to Talk to Girls at Parties.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review30906648">

<div id="review_2667248927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2667248927" />
    <a title="Makrand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80273455-makrand"><img alt="Makrand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594039173p2/80273455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2667248927?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Makrand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Makrand" href="/user/show/80273455-makrand">Makrand</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80273455-makrand?shelf=fantasy-magic-mythology">fantasy-magic-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80273455-makrand?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667248927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1719362042302624303"><i>Seems like a collection of drafts. Some really amazing plots and really wierd ideas as expected of Gaiman's book however lacks the magic of his story telling. </i><br/>____________<br/><br/><b>Fragile Things</b> is a collection of short stories and poems by my favourite author <i>Neil Gaiman</i>.<br/><br/>This would probably be his first book which I disliked and wanted to finish as soon as I can.<br/><br/>Fragile Things majorly consists of spooky, grim tales of deceit, treachery and revenge. What I hated the most was, i felt this was Neil's 'draf</span>
  <span id="freeText1719362042302624303" style="display:none"><i>Seems like a collection of drafts. Some really amazing plots and really wierd ideas as expected of Gaiman's book however lacks the magic of his story telling. </i><br />____________<br /><br /><b>Fragile Things</b> is a collection of short stories and poems by my favourite author <i>Neil Gaiman</i>.<br /><br />This would probably be his first book which I disliked and wanted to finish as soon as I can.<br /><br />Fragile Things majorly consists of spooky, grim tales of deceit, treachery and revenge. What I hated the most was, i felt this was Neil's 'drafts' instead of a book for stories were quite abrupt, with no proper ending or even characters. Lacked the spooky factor. I'd start getting interested in a story and the next moment it would end abruptly just like that.<br /><br />There were around 20-23 short stories/poems and I liked just two or three of them. "Goliath" was my favourite.<br /><br /> The only reason I finished the book was because I wanted to see at what lengths Neil can elaborate his fantasies and I really respect him for that since I believe No one can write Fantasies as Neil does &amp; he sure didn't disappoint me in that area.<br /><br />Read this book for crazy ideas, wierd topics and exceptionally out of the box plots.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1719362042302624303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a6Os9d27cFeQxdl+ifNRptHNYnh/G7fzCkFA6EMUIJqrGKWKfNdAutLpfRXHcSxvJIRFdWsBSshTKA1swWAX/g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nRNA6JqW5pXXlguPW38wWS5DZylkamLj4gVPYItPE01dqEmXO/rWeJW6r+QV/U2Q2wpAJHBwn9i7bALkCTskKQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Snyder did when he joined it;• German atrocities toward captured crew and civilians;• behind-the-scenes stories of the Belgium civilians who risked all to save American flyers who were in the air one moment, spiraling down in flames the next;• creation and dedication of the monument to the Susan Ruth and its crew located in Macquenoise, Belgium in 1989.Shot Down was created from the vast number of letters and journals of Howard Snyder; diaries of men and women on the ground who rescued, sheltered and hid the crew; and interviews conducted by historians. Centered around the 306th Bomb Group in Thurleigh, England, it is informative, insightful and captivating.For most, 70 years is a long time ago. World War II fades in importance as each year goes by. Shot Down moves history out of the footnotes into reality, keeping the stories of real people alive as they experience being shot down. You are there, almost holding your breath as Lt. They were adventurous, smart, and fearless—they were the first women archaeologists. What drew these pioneering ladies into a male-dominated field that was then a very young science? What drove them to travel to far-flung sites where the well water was filled with bugs, danger was daily, and the sun was so hot it could bake through leather boots? Each woman found archaeology to be an irresistible passion. And as they pursued their dreams, they helped to bury ideas about feminine nature as something intrinsically soft and submissive. Ladies of the Field excavates the stories of women who sought adventure in the burgeoning new field of archaelogy and who continue to inspire us today, including Amelia Edwards, Jane Dieulafoy, Zelia
